On 5/29/06, John Jason Jordan <johnxj at comcast.net> wrote:
> On Mon, 29 May 2006 21:06:08 -0700
>
> Another good suggestion for a solution. Except that I'd have to know
> how to edit the grub boot menu from the command line.
>

When you boot the laptop, immediatly after the bios flashes by you may
be presented with a list of options to boot into -- this is where
you'd choose to boot into Windows if your laptop is set up to
dual-boot.  That list will often have entries for all your old
kernels, allowing you to boot into a "last known good" configuration
(of sorts).

If you don't have such an option, then yes, you do need to edit your
grub menu config file, but it's no more scary than the x.org file you
already edited.  (note: you need to edit the grub file *now*, as
_usually_ when you need this option, you *can't* edit the file.)  Just
incase you're concerned about this option interrupting the bootup
process -- typically grub is set to auto-select a default after 3-5
seconds.

Regarding your first email:  You mention using your usb backup and an
old drive to get around your problem, and in that comment you elude to
not knowing how to restore from the backup.  I strongly suggest you
figure out how to do that, and store the step-by-step instructions in
a place you can access them with out using the computer in question.
(Paper works well :).  I make more mistakes when I'm rushed and
harried, which is often the case when restoring backups.

--Rogan

From bobby_miesen at yahoo.com  Tue May 30 01:15:51 2006
From: bobby_miesen at yahoo.com (Robert Miesen)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 01:15:51 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Newbie with an old system
In-Reply-To: <hud9729vjft3pospe25d45f5cf5376q35r@4ax.com>
References: <hud9729vjft3pospe25d45f5cf5376q35r@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <447BFF37.6000306@yahoo.com>

As I was analyzing the command you are using to try and mount your flash 
disk, I noticed that you only gave the name of the device you want to 
mount. This will only work if you have an entry for that device listed 
in /etc/fstab. If you don't, you need to specify some more options to 
mount your disk.

        First, you need to specify the type of the disk being mounted, 
which is specified by using the '-t' option. Second, you need to specify 
the name of the disk you want mounted, which might be /dev/scsi0 in your 
case. Last, you need to spcify where you want your disk mounted. The 
desired directory must exist beforehand. In your case, you might try 
creating a folder in /media called 'Jumpdisk' by using the following 
command from a command shell as root:

#  mkdir /media/Jumpdisk

       The full command to mount your disk should be something like this:

$  mount -t vfat /dev/scsi0 /media/Jumpdisk

       This might not work for regular users because of how secure Linux 
is. If this is the case, you have two options: (1) run the mount command 
as root or (2) append the following line to your /etc/fstab file:

/dev/scsi0      /media/Jumpdisk     vfat    
defaults,shortname=winnt,user   0       0

       This can be quickly accomplished by executing the following 
command from a root shell:

#  echo /dev/scsi0      /media/Jumpdisk     vfat    
defaults,shortname=winnt,user   0       0 >> /etc/fstab


       I would recommend that you take the 2nd option because it permits 
you to use your jumpdisk as a regular user while keeping everyone except 
the root from messing with your jumpdisk.

       I hope this helps. Let me know if my commands don't make sense to 
you. There are NO stupid questions except the ones not asked. ;)

>>>>> "Rogan" == Rogan Creswick <creswick at gmail.com> writes:

Rogan> If you don't have such an option, then yes, you do need to edit
Rogan> your grub menu config file, but it's no more scary than the
Rogan> x.org file you already edited.  (note: you need to edit the
Rogan> grub file *now*, as _usually_ when you need this option, you
Rogan> *can't* edit the file.)

Actually, one of the beautiful things about grub is that it gives you
a command-line where you can do *lots* of things, including edit the
various boot options or compose one entirely new.  You can't save
these, but you can mutate on an adhoc basis all you want.

I just put together a grub boot floppy that configures itself to
operate over a serial console.  This will let me boot up random
hardware without a monitor/keyboard attached as long as the box has a
floppy drive and a serial port.  I'll need to hunt and peck around to
find the right root partition and kernel (grub does filename
completion, so tab is your friend), but it is immensely flexible, and
it'll let me get root on a box that by an oversight I previously did
not have.  You could do the same thing with a CD instead of a floppy.

Grub rocks.

John,

When you install a new kernel (by apt-get install kernel-image***), the 
old kernel is not removed. You can select either kernel to boot from. 
When I upgraded from 2.4. to 2.6, I lost my wifi connection, but booting 
into the old kernel I had it, so it is important to keep the old kernel 
around until you know that everything will work correctly and then 
remove it (by apt-get remove kernel-image-old-one). The more I screw up 
my system the more I know how it all works together and the more I 
install things that are foreign to me like apache and get them to work 
the more I learn.

Christian

From travislspencer at gmail.com  Tue May 30 09:10:29 2006
From: travislspencer at gmail.com (Travis Spencer)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 09:10:29 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Insuring that server comes up in working order
Message-ID: <e3b7bac0605300910j45a148fdu5976b103bf96b5ab@mail.gmail.com>

Hey All,

I'm in charge on an FC4 box here at work but don't have control of
anything else on my employer's network (UPS, other servers, etc.)
Every once and a while the power goes out and taking my machine, DHCP,
and NIS with it.  My server comes up faster than the others making it
inaccessible till I can physically go to it and reboot it.  Does
anyone have a suggestion on how to insure that my server comes up in
working order?  My only idea is to write an init script that sleeps
for 5 minutes that can be bypassed somehow when the extra wait time
isn't needed.  Any thoughts?

-- 

Regards,

Travis Spencer


From plancashire at ci.portland.or.us  Tue May 30 09:17:40 2006
From: plancashire at ci.portland.or.us (Lancashire, Pete)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 09:17:40 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Insuring that server comes up in working order
Message-ID: <9AFECDC22C4D6942BDFFCBDFCDB27A97074ED971@cityemail.bit.city>

if the devices that you depend on being there first
have a network connection, you can test via things
like SNMP for their status. The UPS's that don't
have their own network connection sometimes have
serial<->SNMP options, and there are serial port
drivers as well. some other devices get tricky,
such as CSU/DSUs. There I use to test for something
upstream from them such as a router.

in init.d or equiv. make your script be one that runs
before those that depend on the other stuff being
up. I'm not sure about Linux, but maybe one way to have a 'dont want to wait
flag' set via grub, and make it one of the
options in grubs boot screen

-pete

From plug at merlot.com  Tue May 30 09:58:22 2006
From: plug at merlot.com (Kurt Sussman)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 09:58:22 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Insuring that server comes up in working order
In-Reply-To: <e3b7bac0605300910j45a148fdu5976b103bf96b5ab@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e3b7bac0605300910j45a148fdu5976b103bf96b5ab@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060530165822.GQ24074@merlot.com>

Travis Spencer (travislspencer at gmail.com) typed this ...
> I'm in charge on an FC4 box here at work but don't have control of
> anything else on my employer's network (UPS, other servers, etc.)
> Every once and a while the power goes out and taking my machine, DHCP,
> and NIS with it.  My server comes up faster than the others making it
> inaccessible till I can physically go to it and reboot it.  Does
> anyone have a suggestion on how to insure that my server comes up in
> working order?  My only idea is to write an init script that sleeps
> for 5 minutes that can be bypassed somehow when the extra wait time
> isn't needed.  Any thoughts?

By 'working order' you mean that it gets networking set up, right? 

You can use ifplugd to make sure that everything that needs networking
gets started when the network is available.

If you have a budget for this, use a network power switch and have the
DHCP or NIS server hit the switch to turn your server on after it has
initialized.

--Kurt

> Thanks for answering

> What I done so ?far
> 
> Install Postfix
> 
> Install Apache with PHP
> 
> Install IMAP
> 
> Install SquirrelMail

....

You might need to enter the appropriate PHP modules in httpd.conf. 
Squirrelmail is just a big ole PHP script, so you need to get PHP working 
first. 

Uncomment

#AddType application/x-httpd-php .php
#AddType application/x-httpd-php-source .phps

Then you'll need to configure your usual virtual hosts. Then a nice trick is 
to create a softlink to a /webmail directory, so users can go to 
domain.com/webmail:

# ln -s /usr/share/squirrelmail /var/www/webmail

Squirrelmail installs with a raft of help docs, so be sure to dig them out.

> You might need to enter the appropriate PHP modules in httpd.conf.

> domain.com/webmail:

> Squirrelmail installs with a raft of help docs, so be sure to dig them out.

You can also set up an alias in squirrelmail.conf to take care of
that...

    Alias /webmail /usr/share/squirrelmail

I assume by "localhost/squirrelmail" you mean you're pointing your
browser at http://localhost/squirrelmail as opposed to trying to invoke
it from the command line (nod yes).

You can test to make certain you've got Apache w/PHP configured
correctly by creating the following simple php page (call it
info.php)...

<?php
phpinfo();
?>

...and pointing your browser at it. It should yield a wealth of
information about your PHP configuration.

Sandy

Automate Linux Installations with Debian Pre-Seeding

Automate Linux Installations with Debian Pre-Seeding (Part 2)

The traditional tool for Debian is FAI, which is wickedly difficult to learn.

nicely.

From ianburrell at gmail.com  Tue May 30 11:21:09 2006
From: ianburrell at gmail.com (Ian Burrell)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 11:21:09 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Insuring that server comes up in working order
In-Reply-To: <e3b7bac0605300910j45a148fdu5976b103bf96b5ab@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e3b7bac0605300910j45a148fdu5976b103bf96b5ab@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d91f09cd0605301121q7f7a6e5bg3ce3150b11109fb2@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/30/06, Travis Spencer <travislspencer at gmail.com> wrote:
>
> I'm in charge on an FC4 box here at work but don't have control of
> anything else on my employer's network (UPS, other servers, etc.)
> Every once and a while the power goes out and taking my machine, DHCP,
> and NIS with it.  My server comes up faster than the others making it
> inaccessible till I can physically go to it and reboot it.  Does
> anyone have a suggestion on how to insure that my server comes up in
> working order?  My only idea is to write an init script that sleeps
> for 5 minutes that can be bypassed somehow when the extra wait time
> isn't needed.  Any thoughts?
>

One possibility is to increase the timeout of the DHCP client.  By
default, it is 60 seconds.  If you increased it to 5 minutes, the
client would sit waiting for the DHCP server to respond.  I think the
config file is /etc/dhclient.conf.

The other solution I can think of is have a startup which runs last
and checks if the network and all the services are working.  It would
either restart them by switching runlevels or reboot the whole
machine.

 - Ian

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Tue May 30 12:19:56 2006
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 12:19:56 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] install debian from an image file on server 
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Tue, 30 May 2006 12:03:50 PDT."
	<447C9716.1000109@rocksolidservice.com> 
Message-ID: <20060530192001.F23838F0D@tinman.seitzassoc.com>

Christian Bewley <christian at rocksolidservice.com> wrote:

> 
> 
> Thanks, but I am looking for an easy way to do mass installs from an
> image placed on the server.
> 

Your solution is likely to be similar to the ltsp boot process.  


Client runs some sort of network boot from ROM, typically PXE boot.

Server dhcpd hands client an IP address, tftp server and boot file name.

Client downloads boot file from tftp server.

Client boots from downloaded file.


For your needs the boot file could contain a stripped down kernel and
init whose sole purpose is to pull a disk image from the network and
dd it to the disk.

galen

If you don't have a domain, why would you want to configure
squirrelmail? Its purpose is to allow you to read/send email when you're
away from your server but have access to the web. Do you have a fixed IP
you would use to do that?

As far as IMAP goes, you need to have that configured correctly before
it's useful to squirrelmail. See if this helps...

http://www.squirrelmail.org/wiki/SquirrelMailAndCourierIMap

(assuming you're running courier imap)

Sandy

Good. Fast. Cheap. O'Reilly Launches PDF Guides

As part of O'Reilly Media's commitment to delivering vital technology
information to people who need it, when they need it, O'Reilly is
launching an ongoing series of PDF publications to address cutting edge
technologies. O'Reilly's PDF guides are in-depth, immediate, timely, and
authoritative. Readers can purchase and download the PDFs through the
O'Reilly online store, with no restrictions on the ability to save, copy,
or print them.

The advantages to readers are numerous. O'Reilly authors can disseminate
crucial information as the need arises, without having to wait for enough
material to fill an entire book. Production time is reduced dramatically,
giving IT professionals and others immediate access to the knowledge they
want. Plus, readers can easily search the text, copy and paste handy bits
of code into their applications, and take the PDF with them even when
they're offline. But most importantly, readers won't have to compromise in
their pursuit of timely information--these PDFs provide the high-quality
content for which O'Reilly has come to be known.

This month's PDF offerings are available now:

"Build Tag Clouds in Perl and PHP" by Jim Bumgardner
First popularized by the web sites Flickr, Technorati, and del.icio.us,
these amorphous clumps of words now appear on a slew of web sites as
visual evidence of their membership in the elite corps of "Web 2.0." This
PDF analyzes what is and isn't a tag cloud, offers design tips for using
them effectively, and then shows how to collect tags and display them in
the tag cloud format. Scripts are provided in Perl and PHP.
ISBN: 0-596-52794-2, 46 pages, $9.99 US, $12.99 CAN
http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/tagclouds/


"Web Services on Rails" by Kevin Marshall
In recent years, web services have become increasingly useful to smaller
web site developers.  Thanks to standards like SOAP and XML-RPC as well as
frameworks such as Ruby on Rails, developers can easily create web service
clients and servers with fewer errors. This guide looks at how Ruby on
Rails makes building web service clients and servers simple and fun, with
plenty of working examples and code details so you can see just how
everything works.
ISBN: 0-596-52796-9, 32 pages, $9.99 US, $12.99 CA
http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/websor/


"Atlas UpdatePanel Control" by Bertrand Le Roy and Matt Gibbs
The key to making ASP.NET applications more responsive to user input is
the UpdatePanel control. In this tutorial, you'll learn from the experts:
Bertrand Le Roy, UpdatePanel control's architect and developer, and Matt
Gibbs, Atlas dev team manager. This PDF document contains all you need to
get started implementing AJAX functionality in existing ASP.NET
applications.
ISBN: 0-596-52747-0, 56 pages, $9.99 US, $12.99 CA
http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/atlasupc/


"Search Engine Optimization" by Harold Davis
SEO--short for Search Engine Optimization--is the art, craft, and science
of driving web traffic to web sites. Whether your web site depends on
broad, general traffic, or high-quality, targeted traffic, this PDF has
the tools and information you need to draw more traffic to your site, and
build your bottom line. You?ll learn how to effectively use PageRank and
Google itself--effective use of SEO means understanding how Google works:
how to boost placement in Google search results, how not to offend Google,
and how best to use paid Google programs. You?ll also learn how to best
organize your web pages and web sites, apply SEO analysis tools, establish
effective SEO best practices, and much more.
ISBN: 0-596-52786-1, 41 pages, $9.99 US, $12.99 CA
http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/seo/


Other PDFs from O'Reilly can be found in the O'Reilly Store at:
http://pdfs.oreilly.com

From raanders at acm.org  Tue May 30 16:49:22 2006
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 16:49:22 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Networking commands: debian => sysv: translation 
Message-ID: <447CDA02.5060805@acm.org>

I think I got that subject line worded correct.

I am trying to set up the routing for a linux-server with two network 
interfaces, two subnets, and two routes.

The commands make sense but I'm not sure how to do it in the sysv ( 
Redhat/Fedora/WB/CentOS ) way.  I don't remember ever setting any routes 
using the standard init scripts etc. ( More system magic going on? )

The commands are:

auto eth0
iface eth0 inet static
     address 10.10.64.16
     netmask 255.255.255.0
     network 10.10.64.0
     broadcast 10.10.64.255
     gateway 10.10.64.1
     up /bin/ip route add 10.10.64.0/24 dev eth0 src 10.10.64.16 table 64
     up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.64.1 table 64
     up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64
     post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64

auto eth1
iface eth1 inet static
     address 10.10.68.61
     netmask 255.255.255.0
     network 10.10.68.0
     broadcast 10.10.68.255
     up /bin/ip route add 10.10.68.0/24 dev eth1 src 10.10.68.61 table 68
     up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.68.1 table 68
     up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68
     post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68


TIA,
Rod
-- 


From danielmyoung at gmail.com  Tue May 30 17:11:50 2006
From: danielmyoung at gmail.com (Dan Young)
Date: Tue, 30 May 2006 17:11:50 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Networking commands: debian => sysv: translation
In-Reply-To: <447CDA02.5060805@acm.org>
References: <447CDA02.5060805@acm.org>
Message-ID: <2e42bd9b0605301711w5e6a4d70t591bfadf7dbc5396@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/30/06, Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org> wrote:
> The commands make sense but I'm not sure how to do it in the sysv (
> Redhat/Fedora/WB/CentOS ) way.  I don't remember ever setting any routes
> using the standard init scripts etc. ( More system magic going on? )

The magic all happens in /etc/sysconfig/networking-scripts. The
routing config isn't really well documented, but it uses the "/bin/ip
route" syntax. Not sure about the "ip rule" routing policy parts. The
rest should be something like this:

> auto eth0
> iface eth0 inet static
>      address 10.10.64.16
>      netmask 255.255.255.0
>      network 10.10.64.0
>      broadcast 10.10.64.255
>      gateway 10.10.64.1
>      up /bin/ip route add 10.10.64.0/24 dev eth0 src 10.10.64.16 table 64
>      up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.64.1 table 64
>      up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64
>      post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64

/etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth0
DEVICE=eth0
BOOTPROTO=none
ONBOOT=yes
TYPE=Ethernet
IPADDR=10.10.64.16
NETMASK=255.255.255.0
GATEWAY=10.10.64.1

/etc/sysconfig/network/scripts/route-eth0:
10.10.64.0/24 dev eth0 src 10.10.64.16 table 64
default via 10.10.64.1 table 64

> auto eth1
> iface eth1 inet static
>      address 10.10.68.61
>      netmask 255.255.255.0
>      network 10.10.68.0
>      broadcast 10.10.68.255
>      up /bin/ip route add 10.10.68.0/24 dev eth1 src 10.10.68.61 table 68
>      up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.68.1 table 68
>      up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68
>      post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68

/etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth1:
DEVICE=eth1
ONBOOT=yes
TYPE=Ethernet
IPADDR=10.10.68.61
NETMASK=255.255.255.0
NETWORK=10.10.68.255

/etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/route-eth1:
10.10.68.0/24 dev eth1 src 10.10.68.61 table 68
default via 10.10.68.1 table 68

-- 
Dan

>>>>> "Robert" == Robert Miesen <bobby_miesen at yahoo.com> writes:

Robert> Hi all.  Recently I decided to switch from Fedora Core 5 to
Robert> Debian Etch v3.1 and thus far, I am happy with my decision to
Robert> do so. The only real difficulty I am having with Debian is
Robert> that I don't know how to get my Atheros card to work
Robert> correctly. Does anyone know how to detect and install a new
Robert> interface for my wireless card--preferably by using a command?
Robert> I've installed the most recent version of madwifi-ng-tools
Robert> package from debian-unstable distribution.

If you are just using client mode, i've found madwifi-old to be quite
stable.  Check out the svn snapshot and build against your current
kernel.  See: 

  <http://www.madwifi.org/>

and 

  <http://madwifi.org/wiki/UserDocs/GettingMadwifi>

madwifi-ng is relatively unstable and, depending on what you're doing,
panics the kernel from time to time.

In-Reply-To: <2e42bd9b0605301711w5e6a4d70t591bfadf7dbc5396@mail.gmail.com>
References: <447CDA02.5060805@acm.org>
	<2e42bd9b0605301711w5e6a4d70t591bfadf7dbc5396@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <447DA429.2070109@acm.org>

Dan Young wrote:
> On 5/30/06, Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org> wrote:
> 
>> The commands make sense but I'm not sure how to do it in the sysv (
>> Redhat/Fedora/WB/CentOS ) way.  I don't remember ever setting any routes
>> using the standard init scripts etc. ( More system magic going on? )
> 
> 
> The magic all happens in /etc/sysconfig/networking-scripts. The
> routing config isn't really well documented, but it uses the "/bin/ip
> route" syntax. Not sure about the "ip rule" routing policy parts. The
> rest should be something like this:

Dan.  Thank you.  It was the route-ethx information I missed seeing.

Well a closer look shows the script is suppose to be in a non-existant 
directory.  '/etc/sysconfig/network/scripts/' doesn't exist on any of 
the ( Redhat/Fedora/CentOS ) systems I've checked ( so far. )

I can't even find how those files would be called.  I do remember from 
years ago there being a route in init.d but a quick check on a couple of 
systems doesn't find it any more.  The rpm database shows an iproute.

Any other suggestions or places to look?  I'll start the Google searches 
now that I have a clue as to what I'm looking for.

Again thanks,
Rod
-- 

> 
>> auto eth0
>> iface eth0 inet static
>>      address 10.10.64.16
>>      netmask 255.255.255.0
>>      network 10.10.64.0
>>      broadcast 10.10.64.255
>>      gateway 10.10.64.1
>>      up /bin/ip route add 10.10.64.0/24 dev eth0 src 10.10.64.16 table 64
>>      up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.64.1 table 64
>>      up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64
>>      post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.64.0/24 table 64
> 
> 
> /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth0
> DEVICE=eth0
> BOOTPROTO=none
> ONBOOT=yes
> TYPE=Ethernet
> IPADDR=10.10.64.16
> NETMASK=255.255.255.0
> GATEWAY=10.10.64.1
> 
> /etc/sysconfig/network/scripts/route-eth0:
> 10.10.64.0/24 dev eth0 src 10.10.64.16 table 64
> default via 10.10.64.1 table 64
> 
>> auto eth1
>> iface eth1 inet static
>>      address 10.10.68.61
>>      netmask 255.255.255.0
>>      network 10.10.68.0
>>      broadcast 10.10.68.255
>>      up /bin/ip route add 10.10.68.0/24 dev eth1 src 10.10.68.61 table 68
>>      up /bin/ip route add default via 10.10.68.1 table 68
>>      up /bin/ip rule add from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68
>>      post-down /bin/ip rule delete from 10.10.68.0/24 table 68
> 
> 
> /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth1:
> DEVICE=eth1
> ONBOOT=yes
> TYPE=Ethernet
> IPADDR=10.10.68.61
> NETMASK=255.255.255.0
> NETWORK=10.10.68.255
> 
> /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/route-eth1:
> 10.10.68.0/24 dev eth1 src 10.10.68.61 table 68
> default via 10.10.68.1 table 68
>

> href=/pagename.html>. When that link is selected, the new page loads in the
> browser.
> 
>    However, I cannot get the same behavior locally. I just copied the site
> from one local directory to /var/www/htdocs/appl-ecosys/, but when I point my
> browser at index.html there, that's all that will load.
>

> directory. On the production server that's ../public_html/ while on the
> development server it's one directory higher in the food chain:
> ../htdocs/.
> 
>    Is there a way for me to refernce additional pages, the image and
> publications subdirectories, and include files so that the whole site
> displays properly in both places?

If you change all of your referances from absolute paths to relative
paths, it will display correctly in just about any environment.

From raanders at acm.org  Wed May 31 08:27:07 2006
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Wed, 31 May 2006 08:27:07 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Correct Web Page References on Two Servers
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0605301920510.13135@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0605301920510.13135@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <447DB5CB.30606@acm.org>

Rich Shepard wrote:
>   My web site is hosted by my ISP, and the directory is ~/public_html/. In
> the css menus, individual pages are referenced from the calling page as <a
> href=/pagename.html>. When that link is selected, the new page loads in the
> browser.
> 
>   However, I cannot get the same behavior locally. I just copied the site
> from one local directory to /var/www/htdocs/appl-ecosys/, but when I 
> point my
> browser at index.html there, that's all that will load.

Correct.  Because /index.html is looked for as 
/var/www/htdocs/index.html and all absolute ( httpd ) paths start at 
/var/www/htdocs.

As Derek says you can change to relative paths.  You couldalso put all 
the files in /var/www/htdocs/appl-ecosys/ into /var/www/htdocs/ and your 
absolute paths _should_ work.

>   If I recall correctly, the absolute path is relative to the document root
> directory. On the production server that's ../public_html/ while on the
> development server it's one directory higher in the food chain:
> ../htdocs/.
> 
>   Is there a way for me to refernce additional pages, the image and
> publications subdirectories, and include files so that the whole site
> displays properly in both places?

HTH,
Rod
-- 

> TIA,
> 
> Rich
>

Rich Shepard wrote:
>    I'm going with blosxom <http://www.blosxom.com/>. A single, 444-line perl
> script with a lot of flexibility and plugins available. No dbms back end, no
> php; easy for an amateur like me.

Careful there, a light implementation does not translate into an "easy for an
amateur like me" to use application.

Warning #1:  the date stamps of your files determines the blog order.  Copy some
files around and your blog changes article ordering.

Perhaps a stronger hint comes from http://blosxom.org/blog/ which has a banner
that reads:

  blog about blosxom powered by Movable Type

Michael "former blosxom user" R

                                 PRESENTATION

                              Rapid Discussions

                                      on

                                  Any Topic

                                      by

                              Anyone & Everyone

      Instead of having a formal presentation, we will get together and
      discuss anything anyone wants to discuss in brief sessions of no 
      more than a few minutes each.  If we have enough people involved
      we can break into smaller groups to handle each topic.  David 
      Mandel will provide a structure to make this work and come 
      prepared to discuss one or two of his favorite hacks from 
      Linux Server Hacks.  This should get us started.

      *******************************************************************

"Michael M." <nixlists at writemoore.net> dijo:

> John Jason Jordan wrote

> You can't play DVDs with the open-source nv driver?  Works fine for me.
> 
> I was under the impression the only thing the proprietary driver was 
> good for was 3D acceleration.  I've not bothered with it myself.  This 
> machine came with the proprietary driver pre-installed, but I never

I never noticed any 3-D acceleration, but I don't think I have anything
installed that uses 3-D anyway. As for the "nv" driver and DVDs, I
tried for months, scouring every how-to, wiki page and Linux/Ubuntu
forum for the secret to getting DVDs to play. I tried Totem, VLC, and
several others. Some would launch and just do nothing. Others would
lauch and immediately disappear from the screen. Sometimes I could see
an error message just half a second before they disappeared, but too
fast to read it. I tried launching from the command line, but never got
an error message.

I had heard from several that such problems with Ubuntu-64 could be
resolved by installing the Nvidia propietary drivers, but the
instructions I found were just too daunting. Pages of instructions.
Finally one day I found instructions for installing the Nvidia drivers
that were simple and easy to follow. I did it, and thereafter Totem
played DVDs flawlessly.

So now I'm gonna reinstall them from the same instructions. :)

With any version of squid from 2.4 stable 6 up to the current
stable version compiled from source, trying to start the daemon 
bombs out with signal 6.  I'm wondering if there are special 
configure options that I need to know about.  I'm using a 2.6 
kernel, but with the 2.4.29 headers.  Is it compiling to the 
old headers and not working for that reason?

I'm trying to compile and run squid on an NFS root mounted Slackware 10.1 
system running on a K62-300 VIA VA503+ mobo.  The only thing I can get
working is squid -z.

In var/log/messages:
May 30 22:23:56 condor squid[28042]: Squid Parent: child process 28053 started
May 30 22:23:56 condor squid[28042]: Squid Parent: child process 28053 exited
due to signal 6

The following is what I run to do the configure step:
CC="gcc" \
CFLAGS="-O3 -march=k6" \
./configure \
--prefix=/usr \
--exec-prefix=/usr \
--bindir=/usr/sbin \
--libexecdir=/usr/lib/squid \
--localstatedir=/var \
--sysconfdir=/etc/squid \
--enable-delay-pools \
--enable-cache-digests \
--enable-poll \
--disable-ident-lookups \
--enable-truncate \
--enable-removal-policies="heap" \
--enable-xmalloc-statistics \
--enable-cachemgr-hostname=www \
--enable-linux-netfilter \
--enable-stacktraces

 Squid-2.5.STABLE14 is the version I'm trying to compile and run on
 Slackware 10.1.

Googling a lot, it appears that people who can get squid to compile and
run on redhat/fedora/etc. frequently can't get it to work
on slackware.  I'd rather not switch from slackware to say CentOS because
of how easy it is to get slackware to network boot in comparison, but I
am at a total and complete loss.

BTW: Where are squid's configure options documented?  The INSTALL and
     QUICKSTART offer no information about configure options.

Is a patch needed to make squid work on slackware?  Is pam required?

This is what I'm using as an rc file:
#!/bin/sh
# nome del file: /etc/rc.d/rc.squid
echo -n ' squid '
case "$1" in
start)
/usr/sbin/squid -D
;;
stop)
/usr/sbin/squid -k shutdown
;;
restart)
/usr/sbin/squid -k reconfigure
;;
*)
echo "Usage: `basename $0` {start|stop|restart}"
;;
esac
#
# EOF (c) 2005 Stefano Tagliaferri - GPL license

Subject: [PLUG] UW-Imap not running...
Message-ID: <1149056969.447d37c939450@xerxes.robinson-west.com>

Firewalled off or blocked by tcp wrappers is a strong possibility.

Make sure you have visibility for squirrelmail.  If you are running
uw-imap on an ip address you have no route to from squirrelmail, it
definitely won't work.

One problem I'd run into with UW-IMAP is that it would crash when
it ran into non mail files and tried to treat them as such.

Blithely picking a domain name does not strike me as a very good
idea.  This is one of the major downsides of ip networking and
why it's too bad that everything is going to it.  People use 
unregistered names on private networks only to get in trouble
when they interact with the Internet.  The Internet domain system
was not designed with private networks in mind.  Indeed, ipv6 is
trying to make available a global ip for every computer on the
planet.  As far as finding names for that many ip addresses, unique
ones that is, good luck.  One approach to the problem is redesigning 
the resolver libraries so that you can set up your own private dns 
hierarchy that is not related to the Internet system.  Another 
meaningful approach is to set up smtp servers that work like squid 
instead of using ip masquerading to go beyond your private lan.

My tip is to find out what root domain names will never be used on the
Internet and look into naming private hosts with those domains.  For
consideration, will .pri ever be an Internet domain?  How about .cox,
.lan, .home, etc?  Using a private domain name internally and 
still managing to interact properly with the Internet, that's the real 
challenge.  I use a registered name internally and externally because
I don't know how to set up my MTA otherwise.  I doubt it's the best way 
to do things, have two different ip addresses in two distinct
networks for the same name.  Where trouble arises is when the headers
of your email repeat the same hostname twice in a row.

The problem I see with TCP/IP networking is that the protocols seem
to be designed from the mindset that they will serve clients on one huge
network.  This is rarely true in today's day and age.  With the shortage
of address space on the Internet, most organizations and individuals are
purusing network address translation to conserve address space, save money,
and ensure privacy.  IPv6's designers should have focused on this fact in
my opinion.  After all, you don't make all your private hosts directly
accessible from the Internet even if they are connected to it.  The other
gripe I have with IPv6 is that it's still experimental and I question if
it is going to be a true drop in replacement for IPv4 without obsoleting 
much of the installed IPv4 infrastructure.

I do not know how to enforce going from more restrictive tcp wrappers to less
restrictive ones without rebooting.  This is a common source of trouble when
setting up email servers.

Practically speaking, name shortage is a problem that will not be solved by
increasing the size of the ip address space.  There are only so many unique
names that aren't obnoxiously long.  I'm curious what is going to happen in 
the future when the available names are exhausted?

# netstat -nlpt

The latter at a root prompt will give you your tcp service ports, 
look for 143.

Internetwork name resolution is one area where I have great difficulty.
I would recommend using IPX/SPX instead of TCP/IP to implement a
private local area network except for the fact that IPX/SPX isn't 
free.

Get php webmail working checklist:
    0) Relevant IP routing, tcp wrappers, and firewalls configured.
    1) Name resolution is functioning properly.
    2) Imap server set up and working.
    3) Apache up and php functional.
    4) Webmail software installed and configured.

For many webmail programs, setting up your email system without it is a
prerequisite to using it.

I allowed Internet access to a webmail program on a web site for a while,
but it was too easily abused.  I now know that a jerk used eblaster
on a friend's computer to hijack our clear text transactions.  
Something to keep in mind, do you like webmail better than say, 
evolution or pine even?  Remote access via secure tunneling is something 
to seriously consider as a much more secure alternative.  I don't know
how to do this, but secret key authentication in place of passwords
could also be more secure.  You could carry the key on say a thumb
drive and replace it with a new secret every week or so.

Regards,

Michael C. Robinson

Has anyone here modified the original XBOX to run Linux?  How does 
Microsoft's XBOX Live online system know that you've altered a unit?  
What is a modchip?  Does going the modchip route really allow someone 
to hide that their XBOX is Linux ready from Microsoft?  How does an 
ITX form factor Celeron compare to the XBOX as far as: running quietly 
and taking up very little space?

Why is XBOX so popular if it's nothing more than a low end PC that has 
been hardware modified so that it can run the XBOX operating system only?

Why modify an XBOX to run Linux instead of going with a Micro-ATX
or ITX form factor PC?  Isn't buying one encouraging the rage over
these things by giving them resale value?

On the other hand, there must be some reason why there are instructions
online on how to make these things run Linux.
